rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1239400231">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .navbar li a abbr{color:var(--color-base)!important}@media(prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .navbar li a abbr{color:var(--color-base)!important}}@media print{.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:none!important}}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Shia_Islam" title="Template:Shia Islam"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Shia_Islam" title="Template talk:Shia Islam"><abbr title="Discuss this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Karbala</b><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is a city in central <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, located about 100&#160;km (62&#160;mi) southwest of <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, and a few miles east of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Milh" title="Lake Milh">Lake Milh</a>, also known as Razzaza Lake.<sup id="cite_ref-Risk2008_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Risk2008-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UF2004_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UF2004-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Karbala is the capital of <a href="/wiki/Karbala_Governorate" title="Karbala Governorate">Karbala Governorate</a>, and has an estimated population of 691,100 people (2024).<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>The city, best known as the location of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Karbala" title="Battle of Karbala">Battle of Karbala</a> in 680&#160;AD, or for the <a href="/wiki/Shrine" title="Shrine">shrines</a> of <a href="/wiki/Imam_Husayn_Shrine" class="mw-redirect" title="Imam Husayn Shrine">Hussain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Abbas_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Abbas Mosque">Abbas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Shimoni_&amp;_Levine,_1974,_p._160_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shimoni_&amp;_Levine,_1974,_p._160-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Aghaie,_2004,_pp._10-11_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aghaie,_2004,_pp._10-11-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is considered a <a href="/wiki/Holy_city" title="Holy city">holy city</a> for <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia Muslims</a>. Tens of millions of Shi'ite Muslims visit the site twice a year. <sup id="cite_ref-Islam_in_the_World_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Islam_in_the_World-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Routledge_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Routledge-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zondervan_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zondervan-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The martyrdom of <a href="/wiki/Husayn_ibn_Ali" title="Husayn ibn Ali">Husayn ibn 'Ali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abbas_ibn_Ali" title="Abbas ibn Ali">Abbas ibn 'Ali</a> 
is commemorated annually by near a hundred million of Shi'ites in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Islam_in_the_World_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Islam_in_the_World-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Routledge_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Routledge-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zondervan_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zondervan-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Up to 34 million pilgrims visit the city to observe <i><a href="/wiki/Ashura" title="Ashura">ʿĀshūrāʾ</a></i> (the tenth day of <a href="/wiki/Muharram" title="Muharram">Muharram</a>), which marks the anniversary of Husayn's death, but the main event is the <i><a href="/wiki/Arbaeen" class="mw-redirect" title="Arbaeen">Arbaʿeen</a></i> (the 40th day after 'Ashura'), where up to 40 million visit the graves. Most of the pilgrims travel on foot and come from all around Iraq and more than 56 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Etymology">Etymology</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1251242444">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px 0;overflow:hidden;width:238px;border-collapse:collapse;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em}.mw-parser-output .ambox-speedy{border-left:10px solid #b32424;background-color:#fee7e6}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em 0.5em;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image{border:none;padding:2px 0 2px 0.5em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-imageright{border:none;padding:2px 0.5em 2px 0;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-empty-cell{border:none;padding:0;width:1px}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image-div{width:52px}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .ambox{display:none!important}}</style><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Karbala" title="Special:EditPage/Karbala">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>&#32;in this section. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2023</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>There are many opinions among different investigators, as to the origin of the word <i>Karbala</i>. Some have pointed out that <i>Karbala</i> has a connection to the "Karbalato" language, while others attempt to derive the meaning of word by analyzing its spelling and language.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (October 2023)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> They conclude that it originates from the "Kar Babel" group of ancient Babylonian villages that included Nainawa, Al-Ghadiriyya, Karbella (or Karb Illu), Al-Nawaweess, and Al-Heer. This last name is today known as Al-Hair and is where <a href="/wiki/Husayn_ibn_Ali" title="Husayn ibn Ali">Husayn</a> ibn Ali's grave is located.
</p><p>The investigator <a href="/wiki/Yaqut_al-Hamawi" title="Yaqut al-Hamawi">Yaqut al-Hamawi</a> had pointed out that the meaning of <i>Karbala</i> could have several explanations, one of which is that the place where Husayn ibn Ali was martyred is made of soft earth—<span title="Arabic-language romanization"><i lang="ar-Latn">al-Karbalāt</i></span>.
</p><p>According to Shia's belief, the archangel <a href="/wiki/Gabriel" title="Gabriel">Gabriel</a> narrated the true meaning of the name <i>Karbala</i> to <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>: a combination of <span title="Arabic-language romanization"><i lang="ar-Latn">karb</i></span> (Arabic: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">كَرْب</span>, "the land which will cause many agonies") and <span title="Arabic-language romanization"><i lang="ar-Latn">balāʾ</i></span> (Arabic: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">بَلاء</span>, "afflictions").<sup id="cite_ref-kamil01_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kamil01-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Religious_significance">Religious significance</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Religious significance"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Dhu_al-Kifl" title="Dhu al-Kifl">Dhu al-Kifl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harut_and_Marut" title="Harut and Marut">Harut and Marut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idris_(prophet)" title="Idris (prophet)">Idris (prophet)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noah_in_Islam" title="Noah in Islam">Noah in Islam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_Babel_in_Islamic_tradition" class="mw-redirect" title="Tower of Babel in Islamic tradition">Tower of Babel in Islamic tradition</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Meso2mil-English.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Meso2mil-English.JPG/220px-Meso2mil-English.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="228" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Meso2mil-English.JPG/330px-Meso2mil-English.JPG 1.5x, href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> in the 3rd millennium BCE, showing <a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">Nineveh</a> (the township of <a href="/wiki/Jonah_in_Islam" title="Jonah in Islam">Yunus</a>)),<sup id="cite_ref-qref&#124;10&#124;98&#124;b=y_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qref|10|98|b=y-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IbnHisham,_V.1,_P.419–421_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IbnHisham,_V.1,_P.419–421-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SycOrth_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SycOrth-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tell_al-Rimah" title="Tell al-Rimah">Qattara (or Karana)</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C5%ABr-Katlimmu" class="mw-redirect" title="Dūr-Katlimmu">Dūr-Katlimmu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assur" title="Assur">Assur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arrapha" title="Arrapha">Arrapha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terqa" title="Terqa">Terqa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuzi" title="Nuzi">Nuzi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mari,_Syria" title="Mari, Syria">Mari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eshnunna" title="Eshnunna">Eshnunna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dur-Kurigalzu" title="Dur-Kurigalzu">Dur-Kurigalzu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Der_(Sumer)" title="Der (Sumer)">Der</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sippar" title="Sippar">Sippar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">Babylon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kish_(Sumer)" title="Kish (Sumer)">Kish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Susa" title="Susa">Susa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borsippa" title="Borsippa">Borsippa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nippur" title="Nippur">Nippur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isin" title="Isin">Isin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uruk" title="Uruk">Uruk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Larsa" title="Larsa">Larsa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ur" title="Ur">Ur</a>, from north to south. Note the relative proximity of Babylon and Sippar to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Milh" title="Lake Milh">Lake Milh</a>, which is near Karbala.<sup id="cite_ref-Risk2008_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Risk2008-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UF2004_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UF2004-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure><p>Mesopotamia has been mentioned in Quran. Some Shi'ites consider this verse of the <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a> to refer to Iraq, the land of the Shi'ite sacred sites of <a href="/wiki/Kufa" title="Kufa">Kufah</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Tabatabaei1979_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tabatabaei1979-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kamil2008_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kamil2008-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Najaf, Karbala, <a href="/wiki/Kadhimiyyah" class="mw-redirect" title="Kadhimiyyah">Kadhimiyyah</a><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>b<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Samarra" title="Samarra">Samarra</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-AI2006_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AI2006-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC2007Unesco_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2007Unesco-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> since the <a href="/wiki/Tauhid" class="mw-redirect" title="Tauhid">Monotheistic</a> preachers <a href="/wiki/Abraham_in_Islam" title="Abraham in Islam">Ibrāhīm</a> (<a href="/wiki/Abraham" title="Abraham">Abraham</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Lot_in_Islam" title="Lot in Islam">Lūṭ</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lot_(biblical_person)" title="Lot (biblical person)">Lot</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-qref&#124;26&#124;160&#124;b=y_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qref|26|160|b=y-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> who are regarded as <a href="/wiki/Prophets_in_Islam" class="mw-redirect" title="Prophets in Islam">Prophets in Islam</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Wheeler2002_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wheeler2002-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are believed to have lived in the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Iraq">ancient Iraqi</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Kutha" title="Kutha">Kutha Rabba</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MAH_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MAH-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> before going to "<a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">The Blessed Land</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-qref&#124;21&#124;51&#124;b=y&#125;_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qref|21|51|b=y}-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1244412712">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;margin-top:0}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{padding-left:1.6em}}</style></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Then We delivered him(Ibrahim), along with Lot, to the land We had showered with blessings for all people.</p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8202;<cite><a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://quran.com/21?startingVerse=71">21:71</a></cite></div></blockquote>
<p>Aside from the story of Abraham and Lot in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Mesopotamian_polytheism" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Mesopotamian polytheism">Polytheistic</a><sup id="cite_ref-Brit,_AMR_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brit,_AMR-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MAH_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MAH-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-qref&#124;21&#124;51&#124;b=y&#125;_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qref|21|51|b=y}-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> there are passages in the Quran about <a href="/wiki/Mount_Judi" title="Mount Judi">Mount Judi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-qref&#124;11&#124;44&#124;b=y_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qref|11|44|b=y-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-qref&#124;23&#124;23&#124;b=y_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qref|23|23|b=y-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lewis1984_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis1984-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Babil" class="mw-redirect" title="Babil">Babil</a> ("Babylon")<sup id="cite_ref-qref&#124;2&#124;102&#124;b=y_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qref|2|102|b=y-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JE_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JE-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Nineveh" title="Nineveh">Qaryat Yunus</a></i> ("Town of <a href="/wiki/Jonah_in_Islam" title="Jonah in Islam">Jonah</a>").<sup id="cite_ref-qref&#124;10&#124;98&#124;b=y_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qref|10|98|b=y-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IbnHisham,_V.1,_P.419–421_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IbnHisham,_V.1,_P.419–421-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SycOrth_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SycOrth-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The tomb of the martyred Imam has acquired great significance in <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shia</a> tradition because he and his fellow martyrs are seen as models of jihad in the way of God. Shi'ites believe that Karbala is one of the holiest places on Earth according to the following traditions (among others):
</p><p>The angel <a href="/wiki/Gabriel" title="Gabriel">Gabriel</a> narrated to <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a> that:<sup id="cite_ref-kamil01_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kamil01-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1244412712"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Karbala, where your <a href="/wiki/Hussein_ibn_Ali" class="mw-redirect" title="Hussein ibn Ali">grandson</a> and his family will be martyred, is one of the most blessed and the most sacred lands on Earth, and it is one of the valleys of Paradise.</p></blockquote>
<p>The fourth <a href="/wiki/Imamah_(Shia_doctrine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Imamah (Shia doctrine)">Shi'ite Imam</a>, that is <a href="/wiki/Ali_al-Sajjad" title="Ali al-Sajjad">Zayn al-Abidin</a> narrated:<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1244412712"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>God chose the land of Karbalā' as a safe and blessed sanctuary twenty-four thousand years before He created the land of the <a href="/wiki/Ka%27bah" class="mw-redirect" title="Ka&#39;bah">Ka'bah</a> and chose it as a sanctuary. Verily it (Karbala) will shine among the gardens of Paradise like a shining star shines among the stars for the people of Earth.</p></blockquote>
<p>In this regard, <a href="/wiki/Ja%27far_al-Sadiq" title="Ja&#39;far al-Sadiq">Ja'far al-Sadiq</a> narrates, 'Allah, the Almighty, has made the dust of my ancestor's grave – Imam Husain (r.a) as a cure for every sickness and safety from every fear.'<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is narrated from Ja'far that: "The earth of the pure and holy grave of Husayn ibn ‘Ali (r.a) is a pure and blessed musk. For those who consume it, it is a cure for every ailment, and if our enemy uses it then he will melt the way fat melts, when you intend to consume that pure earth recite the following supplication"<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Battle_of_Karbala">Battle of Karbala</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Battle of Karbala"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Karbala" title="Battle of Karbala">Battle of Karbala</a></div>
<p>The Battle of Karbala was fought on the bare deserts on the way to Kufa on October 10, 680 AD (10 Muharram 61 AH). Both <a href="/wiki/Husayn_ibn_Ali" title="Husayn ibn Ali">Husayn ibn Ali</a> and his brother <a href="/wiki/Abbas_ibn_Ali" title="Abbas ibn Ali">Abbas ibn Ali</a> were buried by the local Banī Asad tribe, at what later became known as the <i>Mashhad Al-Husayn</i>. The battle itself occurred as a result of Husain's refusal of <a href="/wiki/Yazid_I" title="Yazid I">Yazid</a>'s demand for allegiance to his caliphate. The Kufan governor, Ubaydallah ibn Ziyad, sent thirty thousand horsemen against Husayn as he traveled to <a href="/wiki/Kufa" title="Kufa">Kufa</a>.  Husayn had no army, he was with his family and few friends who joined them, so there were around 73 men, including the 6-month-old <a href="/wiki/Ali_al-Asghar_ibn_Husayn" title="Ali al-Asghar ibn Husayn">Ali Asghar</a>, son of Imam Husayn, in total. The horsemen, under 'Umar ibn Sa'd, were ordered to deny Husayn and his followers water to force Husayn to agree to give an oath of allegiance. On the 9th of Muharram, Husayn refused, and requested to be given the night to pray. On the 10th day of Muharram, Husayn ibn Ali prayed the morning prayer and led his troops into battle along with his brother Abbas. Many of Husayn's followers, including all of his present sons <a href="/wiki/Ali_al-Akbar_ibn_Husayn" title="Ali al-Akbar ibn Husayn">Ali Akbar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ali_al-Asghar_ibn_Husayn" title="Ali al-Asghar ibn Husayn">Ali Asghar</a> (six months old) and his nephews Qassim, Aun and Muhammad were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 63&#160;AH (683&#160;AD), Yazid ibn Mu'awiya released the surviving members of Husayn's family from prison as there was a threat of uprisings and some of the people in his court were unaware of who the battle was with, when they got to know that the descendants of Muhammad were killed, they were horrified. On their way to Mecca, they stopped at the site of the battle. There is a record of Sulayman ibn Surad going on pilgrimage to the site as early as 65 AH (685 AD). The city began as a tomb and shrine to <a href="/wiki/Husayn_ibn_Ali" title="Husayn ibn Ali">Husayn ibn Ali</a>, grandson of <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a> and son of <a href="/wiki/Ali_ibn_Abi_Talib" class="mw-redirect" title="Ali ibn Abi Talib">Ali ibn Abi Talib</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Seyyed_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seyyed-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and grew as a city to meet the needs of pilgrims. The city and tombs were greatly expanded by successive Muslim rulers, but suffered repeated destruction from attacking armies. The original shrine was destroyed by the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid" class="mw-redirect" title="Abbasid">Abbasid</a> Caliph <a href="/wiki/Al-Mutawakkil" title="Al-Mutawakkil">Al-Mutawakkil</a> in 850 but was rebuilt in its present form around 979, only to be partly destroyed by fire in 1086 and rebuilt yet again.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Early_modern">Early modern</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early modern"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Like <a href="/wiki/Najaf" title="Najaf">Najaf</a>, the city suffered from severe water shortages that were only resolved in the early 18th century by building a dam at the head of the Husayniyya Canal. In 1737, the city replaced <a href="/wiki/Isfahan_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Isfahan (city)">Isfahan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> as the main center of Shia scholarship. In the mid-eighteenth century it was dominated by the dean of scholarship, <a href="/wiki/Yusuf_Al_Bahrani" class="mw-redirect" title="Yusuf Al Bahrani">Yusuf Al Bahrani</a>, a key proponent of the <a href="/wiki/Akhbari" title="Akhbari">Akhbari</a> tradition of Shia thought, until he died in 1772,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> after which the more state-centric <a href="/wiki/Usuli" class="mw-redirect" title="Usuli">Usuli</a> school became more influential.
</p><p><br />
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Wahhabi_sack_of_Karbala" title="Wahhabi sack of Karbala">Wahhabi sack of Karbala</a> occurred on 21 April 1802 (1216 Hijri) (1801),<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> under the rule of <a href="/wiki/Abdul-Aziz_bin_Muhammad" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdul-Aziz bin Muhammad">Abdul-Aziz bin Muhammad</a> the second ruler of the <a href="/wiki/First_Saudi_State" class="mw-redirect" title="First Saudi State">First Saudi State</a>, when 12,000 Wahhabi Muslims from <a href="/wiki/Najd" title="Najd">Najd</a> attacked the city of Karbala.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The attack was coincident with the anniversary of <a href="/wiki/The_event_of_Ghadir_Khumm" class="mw-redirect" title="The event of Ghadir Khumm">Ghadir Khum</a> event,<sup id="cite_ref-Iranica_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iranica-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or 10 <a href="/wiki/Muharram" title="Muharram">Muharram</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Seyyed_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seyyed-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This fight left 3,000–5,000 deaths and the dome of the tomb of <a href="/wiki/Husayn_ibn_Ali" title="Husayn ibn Ali">Husayn ibn Ali</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Seyyed_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seyyed-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> was destroyed.  The fight lasted for 8 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-Alexei_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alexei-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/First_Saudi_State" class="mw-redirect" title="First Saudi State">First Saudi State</a> invasion, the city enjoyed semi-autonomy during Ottoman rule, governed by a group of gangs and mafia variously allied with members of the 'ulama. In order to reassert their authority, the Ottoman army laid siege to the city. On January 13, 1843, Ottoman troops entered the city. Many of the city leaders fled leaving defense of the city largely to tradespeople. About 3,000 Arabs were killed in the city, and another 2,000 outside the walls (this represented about 15% of the city's normal population). The Turks lost 400 men.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This prompted many students and scholars to move to Najaf, which became the main Shia religious centre.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Between 1850 and 1903, Karbala enjoyed a generous influx of money through the <a href="/wiki/Oudh_Bequest" title="Oudh Bequest">Oudh Bequest</a>. The Shia-ruled Indian Province of <a href="/wiki/Awadh" title="Awadh">Awadh</a>, known by the British as Oudh, had always sent money and pilgrims to the holy city. The Oudh money, 10 million rupees, originated in 1825 from the Awadh <a href="/wiki/Nawab" title="Nawab">Nawab</a> <a href="/wiki/Ghazi-ud-Din_Haider" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghazi-ud-Din Haider">Ghazi-ud-Din Haider</a>. One third was to go to his wives, and the other two-thirds went to holy cities of Karbala and Najaf. When his wives died in 1850, the money piled up with interest in the hands of the British <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a>. The EIC sent the money to Karbala and Najaf per the wives' wishes, in the hopes of influencing the <a href="/wiki/Ulama" title="Ulama">Ulama</a> in Britain's favor. This effort to curry favor is generally considered to have been a failure.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Karbala_07402u.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Karbala_07402u.jpg/220px-Karbala_07402u.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Karbala_07402u.jpg/330px-Karbala_07402u.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Karbala_07402u.jpg/440px-Karbala_07402u.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1507" /></a><figcaption>Mosque in Karbala (1932)</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1915, Karbala was the scene of an <a href="/wiki/1915_uprising_in_Karbala" title="1915 uprising in Karbala">uprising against the Ottoman Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1928, an important drainage project was carried out to relieve the city of unhealthy swamps, formed between Hussainiya and the Bani Hassan Canals on the Euphrates.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Defense_of_the_Karbala_City_Hall" title="Defense of the Karbala City Hall">Defense of the City Hall in Karbala</a> – a series of skirmishes fought from April 3 to April 6, 2004, between the Iraqi rebels of the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Companies" class="mw-redirect" title="Peace Companies">Mahdi Army</a> trying to conquer the city hall and the defending Polish and Bulgarian soldiers from the <a href="/wiki/Multinational_Division_Central-South" title="Multinational Division Central-South">Multinational Division Central-South</a>
</p><p>In 2003 following the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">American invasion</a>, the Karbala town council attempted to elect <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">United States Marine Corps</a> <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_colonel_(United_States)" title="Lieutenant colonel (United States)">Lieutenant Colonel</a> Matthew Lopez as mayor. Ostensibly so that his Marines, contractors, and funds could not leave.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On April 14, 2007, a car bomb exploded about 600&#160;ft (180&#160;m) from the shrine to Husayn, killing 47<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and wounding over 150.
</p><p>On January 19, 2008, 2 million <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shia</a> <a href="/wiki/Pilgrim" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilgrim">pilgrims</a> marched through Karbala city, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> to commemorate <a href="/wiki/Day_of_Ashura" class="mw-redirect" title="Day of Ashura">Ashura</a>. 20,000 Iraqi troops and police guarded the event amid tensions due to clashes between Iraqi troops and Shia which left 263 people dead (in <a href="/wiki/Basra" title="Basra">Basra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nasiriya" class="mw-redirect" title="Nasiriya">Nasiriya</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>With an impressive 3.9 million palm trees, Karbala produces approximately 160,000 tons of dates across 90 different varieties.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Karbala has surpassed Saudi Arabia's <a href="/wiki/Al-Ahsa_Oasis" title="Al-Ahsa Oasis">Al-Ahsa Oasis</a>, becoming the world's largest palm oasis.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate">Climate</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Trees_in_Karbala.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Trees_in_Karbala.jpg/220px-Trees_in_Karbala.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Trees_in_Karbala.jpg/330px-Trees_in_Karbala.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Trees_in_Karbala.jpg/440px-Trees_in_Karbala.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="495" /></a><figcaption>Palm trees in Karbala behind a lake</figcaption></figure>
<p>Karbala experiences a <a href="/wiki/Hot_desert_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot desert climate">hot desert climate</a> (<i>BWh</i> in the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>) with extremely hot, long, dry summers and mild winters. Almost all of the yearly precipitation is received between November and April, though no month is wet.
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Karbala is a significant pilgrimage destination for Shia Muslims, especially during the Islamic holy month of Muharram. According to Azher Al-Kalash, Vice President of the Association of Hotels and Tourist Restaurants in Karbala, said, "Karbala has the highest number of hotels in Iraq, with 900 hotels of various levels, equivalent to one-third of the total number of hotels in the entire country. Some hotels have safety and security concerns raised by the civil defense, but the most comply with the regulations and instructions."<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Tourism in every country is influenced by supply and demand. Hence, hotel and transportation prices rise during peak times. In Karbala, the minimum hotel rate is around $10 per night, while the maximum can reach $50 during Ashura. However, the amount doubles during the Arbaeen pilgrimage due to the high demand. Arbaeen is the most significant pilgrimage that hotel owners rely on throughout the year." Thus, tourism plays an important role in stimulating various sectors, whether hotels, agriculture, trade, or others. It contributes to the employment of all economic sectors of society. 
</p><p>Karbala Refinery, with a refining capacity of 140,000 barrels per day (bpd), it stands as Iraq's largest refining project in four decades.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The refinery commenced commercial operations in mid-March 2024, initially operating at 60% capacity, with plans to reach full capacity by August 2024.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is estimated that the refinery produce 70% of country's petroleum products and generate $3bn in revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Religious_tourism">Religious tourism</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Religious tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Shrine_in_Karbala.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Shrine_in_Karbala.jpg/220px-Shrine_in_Karbala.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Shrine_in_Karbala.jpg/330px-Shrine_in_Karbala.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Shrine_in_Karbala.jpg/440px-Shrine_in_Karbala.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="483" /></a><figcaption>Shrine in Karbala, showing use of <a href="/wiki/Arabesque" title="Arabesque">Arabesque</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%AA%D8%A8%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D9%8A%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%85%D9%82%D8%AF%D8%B3%D8%A9_(6).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%AA%D8%A8%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D9%8A%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%85%D9%82%D8%AF%D8%B3%D8%A9_%286%29.jpg/220px-%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%AA%D8%A8%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D9%8A%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%85%D9%82%D8%AF%D8%B3%D8%A9_%286%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%AA%D8%A8%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D9%8A%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%85%D9%82%D8%AF%D8%B3%D8%A9_%286%29.jpg/330px-%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%AA%D8%A8%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D9%8A%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%85%D9%82%D8%AF%D8%B3%D8%A9_%286%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%AA%D8%A8%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D9%8A%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%85%D9%82%D8%AF%D8%B3%D8%A9_%286%29.jpg/440px-%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%AA%D8%A8%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A8%D8%A7%D8%B3%D9%8A%D8%A9_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%85%D9%82%D8%AF%D8%B3%D8%A9_%286%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Al-Abbas_Shrine" title="Al-Abbas Shrine">Al-Abbas Shrine</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Karbala, alongside <a href="/wiki/Najaf" title="Najaf">Najaf</a>, is considered a thriving tourist destination for Shia Muslims and the tourism industry in the city boomed after the end of Saddam Hussein's rule.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some religious tourism attractions include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Al_Abbas_Mosque" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Abbas Mosque">Al Abbas Mosque</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Imam_Husayn_Shrine" class="mw-redirect" title="Imam Husayn Shrine">Imam Husayn Shrine</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Euphrates" title="Euphrates">Euphrates</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ruins_of_Mujada" title="Ruins of Mujada">Ruins of Mujada</a>, about 40&#160;km (25 miles) to the west of the city<sup id="cite_ref-Al-Shirazi_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Al-Shirazi-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Holy_Karbala_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holy_Karbala-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/Arbaeen" class="mw-redirect" title="Arbaeen">Arbaeen</a> is a massive annual pilgrimage event that takes place in Karbala. It is considered one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_peaceful_gatherings" title="List of largest peaceful gatherings">largest peaceful gatherings</a> in the world. In 2017, approximately 30 million people took part in the pilgrimage.
</p><p>The official number of visitors during the 10-day period surpassed 22 million people on September 6, 2023, making it the largest and most peaceful gathering in the world. Shia Muslims largely attended the commemoration, as well as many Sunni Muslims and Christians who also visited to pay their respect to Imam Hussein.
</p><p>Who Is Hussain, a charity is based in Karbala, has accumulated around 50,000 blood donations, saved more than 140,000 lives and helped feed more than 700,000 people. During the period of Arbaeen, its teams provide voluntary initiatives around the world like donating blood, alongside distributing food, drink and masks to citizens, to countries including the United States, France, Britain, Pakistan, Lebanon as well as African and poverty-driven countries.”
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Karbala_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Karbala FC">Karbala FC</a> is a football club based in Karbala. It plays in the premier <a href="/wiki/Iraq_Stars_League" title="Iraq Stars League">Iraq Stars League</a>, the highest division of the Iraqi football league system.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Karbala_International_Stadium" title="Karbala International Stadium">Karbala Sports City</a> located south of Karbala city, is a large <a href="/wiki/Sports_complex" title="Sports complex">sports complex</a> housing the <a href="/wiki/Karbala_International_Stadium" title="Karbala International Stadium">Karbala International Stadium</a> with a capacity of 30,000 spectators, a smaller football stadium with a capacity of 2,000, as well as a football field for training, a swimming hall, and a hotel.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Universities">Universities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Universities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Karbala" title="University of Karbala">University of Karbala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ahlulbait_University_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahlulbait University College">Ahlulbait University College</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/University_of_Karbala" title="University of Karbala">University of Karbala</a>, which was inaugurated on March 1, 2002, is one of the top most universities in Iraq regarding academic administration, human resources, and scientific research.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ahl_al-Bayt_University" title="Ahl al-Bayt University">Ahl al-Bayt University</a> was founded in September 2003 by Dr. Mohsen Baqir Mohammed-Salih Al-Qazwini. The university has six major colleges: College of Law, Arts, Islamic Sciences, Medical &amp; Health Technology, Pharmacy and Dentistry.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Warith al-Anbiya University in Karbala, sponsored by the Imam Husayn Holy Shrine, was established in 2017. It has the faculties of engineering, administration, economics, law and pathology. It received its first batch of students in the academic year 2017–2018.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Hawza_Seminary">Hawza Seminary</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Hawza Seminary"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hawza" title="Hawza">Hawza</a> are Islamic education institutions that are administered under the guidance of a Grand Ayatollah or group of scholars to teach Shia Muslims and guide them through the rigorous journey of becoming an Alim (a religious scholar). Initially Karbala's hawza consisted mostly of <a href="/wiki/Iranian_peoples" title="Iranian peoples">Iranians</a> and Turkish scholars. The death of Sharif-ul-Ulama Mazandarani in 1830 as well as the repression of the Shia population by the Ottomans in 1843 both played a significant role in the relocation of many scholars to the city of <a href="/wiki/Najaf" title="Najaf">Najaf</a> and thus Najaf subsequently became the center of Shia Islamic leadership and education.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Today the Hawza Seminary still exists in Karbala (such as the School of Allamah Bin Fahd) but to a lesser extent in comparison to Najaf.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Infrastructure"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Airports">Airports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Airports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Airports in Karbala include:<sup id="cite_ref-Frbiu_03-2017_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frbiu_03-2017-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Karbala_Northeast_Airport" title="Karbala Northeast Airport">Karbala Northeast Airport</a><sup id="cite_ref-CAPA_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CAPA-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Karbala_International_Airport" title="Karbala International Airport">Karbala International Airport</a><sup id="cite_ref-MEED_2018_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEED_2018-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> (located to the southeast of Karbala)</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Inter-city_high-speed_railway_system">Inter-city high-speed railway system</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Inter-city high-speed railway system"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In February 2024, the Iraqi National Investment Commission (NIC) unveiled a project to construct an inter-city <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed rail</a> connecting the cities of Karbala and <a href="/wiki/Najaf" title="Najaf">Najaf</a>. Once finished, it is set to accommodate up to 25,000 passengers per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="International_relations">International relations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Karbala&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: International relations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
